     1→/**
     2→ * Network Detection and Conditional Content Display
     3→ * Shows BMW-specific content only when accessed from corporate network

     6→
     7→(function() {
     8→    'use strict';
     9→    
    10→    // Global variable to track corporate network status
    11→    let isCorporateNetworkDetected = false;
    12→
    13→    // BMW corporate network detection
    14→    function isCorporateNetwork() {
    15→        // Check if accessing from BMW corporate network indicators
    16→        const hostname = window.location.hostname;
    17→        const host = window.location.host;
    18→        
    19→        // Corporate network indicators
    20→        const corporateIndicators = [
    21→            // Internal IP ranges (adjust as needed)
    22→            /^10\./,
    23→            /^192\.168\./,
    24→            /^172\.(1[6-9]|2[0-9]|3[01])\./,
    25→            // BMW-specific domains
    26→            /bmw\.com$/,
    27→            /bmwgroup\.com$/
    28→        ];
    29→
    30→        // Check hostname against corporate patterns
    31→        for (const pattern of corporateIndicators) {
    32→            if (pattern.test(hostname) || pattern.test(host)) {
    33→                console.log('Corporate network detected via hostname:', hostname);
    34→                return true;
    35→            }
    36→        }
    37→
    38→        // For development/testing - check if we're on GitHub Pages from public internet
    39→        if (hostname.includes('github.io')) {
    40→            console.log('GitHub Pages detected - showing public content');
    41→            return false;
    42→        }
    43→
    44→        // For localhost/127.0.0.1 - default to corporate for testing
    45→        if (hostname === 'localhost' || hostname === '127.0.0.1') {
    46→            console.log('Localhost detected - defaulting to corporate content for testing');
    47→            return true;
    48→        }
    49→
    50→        // Check user agent or other indicators that might suggest corporate network
    51→        // This is a fallback check
    52→        console.log('No corporate network indicators found for hostname:', hostname);
    53→
    54→        // Default to public network if no corporate indicators found
    55→        return false;
    56→    }
    57→
    58→    function checkInternalService() {
    59→        // Run internal service check to detect corporate network access
    60→        console.log('Running internal service check to detect corporate network access');
    61→        
    62→        // Show initial status
    63→        updateNetworkStatusIndicator('checking');
    64→        
    65→        // Try multiple detection methods
    66→        let detectionComplete = false;
    67→        
    68→        // Method 1: URL parameter override REMOVED to prevent manual corporate mode switching
    69→        
    70→        // Method 2: Check external IP first, then try internal service
    71→        console.log('🔍 Checking BMW network access');
    72→        console.log('🌍 Current hostname:', window.location.hostname);
    73→        console.log('🌍 Current URL:', window.location.href);
    74→        
    75→        // Check external IP for BMW ranges (this was working before!)
    76→        fetch('https://api.ipify.org?format=json')
    77→            .then(response => response.json())
    78→            .then(data => {
    79→                console.log('🌐 External IP detected:', data.ip);
    80→                // BMW corporate IP ranges
    81→                const corporateIPPatterns = [
    82→                    /^160\.46\./,    // Your working IP range
    83→                    /^194\.114\./,   // BMW public IP range
    84→                    /^195\.34\./,    // BMW public IP range
    85→                    /^212\.204\./    // BMW public IP range
    86→                ];
    87→                
    88→                const isCorporateIP = corporateIPPatterns.some(pattern => {
    89→                    if (pattern.test(data.ip)) {
    90→                        console.log(`✅ IP ${data.ip} matches corporate pattern: ${pattern}`);
    91→                        return true;
    92→                    }
    93→                    return false;
    94→                });
    95→                
    96→                if (isCorporateIP && !detectionComplete) {
    97→                    console.log('✅ Corporate IP range detected - showing corporate content');
    98→                    detectionComplete = true;
    99→                    showCorporateContent();
   100→                } else if (!detectionComplete) {
   101→                    console.log(`📍 IP ${data.ip} not in corporate ranges, trying internal service check`);
   102→                    tryInternalServiceCheck();
   103→                }
   104→            })
   105→            .catch(error => {
   106→                console.log('❌ IP detection failed, trying internal service check:', error);
   107→                tryInternalServiceCheck();
   108→            });
   109→            
   110→        function tryInternalServiceCheck() {
   111→            if (detectionComplete) return;
   112→            
   113→            // Try internal service check with BMW Content Hub only (no 10.x latency)
   114→            const testUrls = [
   115→                'https://contenthub.bmwgroup.net/favicon.ico'  // BMW Content Hub (most reliable, no VPN latency)
   116→            ];
   117→            
   118→            let urlIndex = 0;
   119→            
   120→            function testNextUrl() {
   121→                if (urlIndex >= testUrls.length || detectionComplete) {
   122→                    // All URLs failed
   123→                    if (!detectionComplete) {
   124→                        console.log('❌ All internal service checks failed - showing public content');
   125→                        hideCorporateContent();
   126→                        detectionComplete = true;
   127→                    }
   128→                    return;
   129→                }
   130→                
   131→                const testUrl = testUrls[urlIndex];
   132→                console.log(`🔍 Trying internal service: ${testUrl}`);
   133→                
   134→                const img = new Image();
   135→                img.onload = function() {
   136→                    if (!detectionComplete) {
   137→                        console.log('✅ Internal service reachable - showing corporate content');
   138→                        showCorporateContent();
   139→                        detectionComplete = true;
   140→                    }
   141→                };
   142→                img.onerror = function() {
   143→                    console.log(`❌ Failed to reach: ${testUrl}`);
   144→                    urlIndex++;
   145→                    setTimeout(testNextUrl, 500); // Try next URL after short delay
   146→                };
   147→                
   148→                img.src = testUrl + '?' + Date.now();
   149→            }
   150→            
   151→            testNextUrl();
   152→        }
   153→        
   154→        // Set a timeout to ensure we don't wait forever  
   155→        setTimeout(() => {
   156→            if (!detectionComplete) {
   157→                console.log('⏱️ BMW ContentHub check timed out after 2s - defaulting to public content');
   158→                hideCorporateContent();
   159→                detectionComplete = true;
   160→            }
   161→        }, 2000);
   162→    }
   163→
   164→    async function showCorporateContent() {
   165→        // Safety check: Only allow corporate content on actual corporate networks
   166→        const hostname = window.location.hostname;
   167→        if (hostname.includes('github.io') || hostname.includes('fwornle')) {
   168→            console.log('🛡️ Corporate content blocked - not on corporate network');
   169→            hideCorporateContent();
   170→            return;
   171→        }
   172→        
   173→        console.log('🏢 Showing BMW corporate content');
   174→        
   175→        // Set global flag to prevent MutationObserver from re-hiding content
   176→        isCorporateNetworkDetected = true;
   177→        
   178→        const corporateElements = document.querySelectorAll('.bmw-corporate-only');
   179→        console.log(`Found ${corporateElements.length} corporate elements to show`);
   180→        corporateElements.forEach((element, index) => {
   181→            console.log(`Corporate element ${index}:`, element.tagName, element.className);
   182→            element.classList.add('show-corporate');
   183→            element.classList.add('corporate-network-detected');
   184→        });
   185→
   186→        const publicElements = document.querySelectorAll('.bmw-public-alternative');

   189→            console.log(`Public element ${index}:`, element.tagName, element.className);
   190→            element.classList.add('hide-public');
   191→        });
   192→
   193→        // Hide public navigation items and show corporate ones
   194→        hidePublicNavigationItems();
   195→        showCorporateNavigationItems();
   196→
   197→        console.log('🏢 Corporate mode: BMW content enabled');
   198→

   201→            console.log('🔐 Loading encrypted corporate content...');
   202→            try {

   269→                    <p><strong>Set up your local development environment:</strong></p>
   270→                    <ol>
   271→                        <li>Install Python 3.11+</li>
   272→                        <li>Clone the repository</li>
   273→                        <li>Install dependencies per module requirements</li>
   274→                        <li>Configure your own LLM API keys</li>
   275→                    </ol>
   276→                `;
   277→            }
   278→        }
   279→    }
   280→
   281→    function updateNetworkStatusIndicator(networkType) {
   282→        // Only show indicator on Setup & Environment pages
   283→        const currentPath = window.location.pathname;
   284→        const isSetupPage = currentPath.includes('00_intro') || 
   285→                           currentPath.includes('setup') || 
   286→                           currentPath.includes('environment') ||
   287→                           currentPath.includes('coder') ||
   288→                           currentPath.includes('llmapi');
   289→        
   290→        // Remove any existing status indicator
   291→        const existingIndicator = document.querySelector('.network-status-indicator');
   292→        if (existingIndicator) {
   293→            existingIndicator.remove();
   294→        }
   295→
   296→        // Don't show indicator if not on setup pages
   297→        if (!isSetupPage) {
   298→            return;
   299→        }
   300→
   301→        // Create new status indicator
   302→        const indicator = document.createElement('div');
   303→        indicator.className = 'network-status-indicator';
   304→        indicator.style.cssText = `
   305→            position: fixed;
   306→            bottom: 20px;
   307→            right: 20px;
   308→            background: ${networkType === 'corporate' ? '#0066cc' : '#28a745'};
   309→            color: white;
   310→            padding: 8px 12px;
   311→            border-radius: 4px;
   312→            font-size: 12px;
   313→            font-weight: bold;
   314→            z-index: 1000;
   315→            box-shadow: 0 2px 8px rgba(0,0,0,0.2);
   316→            font-family: -apple-system, BlinkMacSystemFont, "Segoe UI", Roboto, sans-serif;
   317→        `;
   318→        
   319→        if (networkType === 'corporate') {
   320→            indicator.innerHTML = `
   321→                🏢 BMW Corporate Network
   322→                <div style="font-size: 10px; font-weight: normal; margin-top: 2px;">
   323→                    Cloud Dev Environment Available
   324→                </div>
   325→            `;
   326→        } else if (networkType === 'checking') {
   327→            indicator.innerHTML = `
   328→                🔍 Detecting Network...
   329→                <div style="font-size: 10px; font-weight: normal; margin-top: 2px;">
   330→                    Checking corporate access
   331→                </div>
   332→            `;
   333→            indicator.style.background = '#ffa500';
   334→        } else {
   335→            indicator.innerHTML = `
   336→                🌐 Public Network
   337→                <div style="font-size: 10px; font-weight: normal; margin-top: 2px;">
   338→                    Local Setup Required
   339→                </div>
   340→            `;
   341→        }
   342→
   343→        // Remove manual override clickability to prevent switching to corporate network
   344→        // This was causing unwanted CN switching when viewing publicly
   345→        indicator.style.cursor = 'default';
   346→        indicator.title = networkType === 'corporate' ? 
   347→            'BMW Corporate Network - Cloud Development Environment Available' : 
   348→            'Public Network - Local Setup Required';
   349→
   350→        document.body.appendChild(indicator);
   351→
   352→        // Auto-hide after 5 seconds
   353→        setTimeout(() => {
   354→            if (indicator && indicator.parentNode) {
   355→                indicator.style.transition = 'opacity 0.5s ease';
   356→                indicator.style.opacity = '0';
   357→                setTimeout(() => {
   358→                    if (indicator && indicator.parentNode) {
   359→                        indicator.remove();
   360→                    }
   361→                }, 500);
   362→            }
   363→        }, 5000);
   364→    }
   365→
   366→    function initializeNetworkDetection() {
   367→        // Add CSS for smooth transitions and ensure BMW content is hidden by default on public sites
   368→        const style = document.createElement('style');
   369→        const hostname = window.location.hostname;
   370→        const isPublicSite = hostname.includes('github.io') || hostname.includes('fwornle');
   371→        
   372→        style.textContent = `
   373→            /* Default: hide all conditional content until detection completes */
   374→            .bmw-corporate-only {
   375→                display: none;
   376→                transition: opacity 0.3s ease-in-out;
   377→            }
   378→            .bmw-public-alternative {
   379→                display: none;
   380→                transition: opacity 0.3s ease-in-out;
   381→            }
   382→            /* Show corporate content when detected */
   383→            .bmw-corporate-only.corporate-network-detected {
   384→                display: block;
   385→                animation: fadeIn 0.5s ease-in-out;
   386→            }
   387→            /* Show public content when detected */
   388→            .bmw-public-alternative.public-network-detected {
   389→                display: block;
   390→                animation: fadeIn 0.5s ease-in-out;
   391→            }
   392→            @keyframes fadeIn {
   393→                from { opacity: 0; }
   394→                to { opacity: 1; }
   395→            }
   396→            /* Ensure setup instructions container is visible */
   397→            .setup-instructions {
   398→                min-height: 100px;
   399→            }
   400→        `;
   401→        document.head.appendChild(style);
   402→
   403→        // Default to public content but allow corporate override
   404→        if (isPublicSite) {
   405→            console.log('GitHub Pages detected - checking for corporate access');
   406→            // Don't immediately hide corporate content, let the service check determine it
   407→            // Try the internal service check on GitHub Pages
   408→            // in case someone is accessing from corporate network
   409→            checkInternalService();
   410→            return;
   411→        }
   412→
   413→        // Initial network check
   414→        if (isCorporateNetwork()) {
   415→            console.log('Corporate network detected initially');
   416→            showCorporateContent();
   417→        } else {
   418→            console.log('Public network assumed initially');
   419→            hideCorporateContent();
   420→        }
   421→    }
   422→
   423→    // Initialize when DOM is ready and on every page load
   424→    function runDetection() {
   425→        // Reset detection state for fresh detection on each page
   426→        console.log('🔄 Starting fresh network detection...');
   427→        initializeNetworkDetection();
   428→    }
   429→    
   430→    // Initial run
   431→    if (document.readyState === 'loading') {
   432→        document.addEventListener('DOMContentLoaded', runDetection);
   433→    } else {
   434→        runDetection();
   435→    }
   436→    
   437→    // Set up navigation listeners immediately (not waiting for DOMContentLoaded)
   438→    console.log('🎯 Setting up navigation listeners');
   439→    
   440→    // Watch for URL changes with MutationObserver
   441→    let lastUrl = location.href;
   442→    const observer = new MutationObserver(() => {
   443→        const url = location.href;
   444→        if (url !== lastUrl) {
   445→            lastUrl = url;
   446→            console.log('📍 URL changed to:', url);
   447→            setTimeout(runDetection, 100);
   448→        }
   449→    });
   450→    observer.observe(document.body || document.documentElement, {
   451→        subtree: true, 
   452→        childList: true
   453→    });
   454→    
   455→    // Listen for navigation link clicks (use capturing to catch all clicks)
   456→    document.addEventListener('click', (e) => {
   457→        const link = e.target.closest('a');
   458→        if (link) {
   459→            const href = link.getAttribute('href');
   460→            console.log('🔗 Link clicked:', href);
   461→            if (link.classList.contains('md-nav__link') || 
   462→                link.classList.contains('md-tabs__link') ||
   463→                href?.includes('/00_intro/')) {
   464→                console.log('🔗 Navigation link detected, will re-run detection');
   465→                setTimeout(runDetection, 500);
   466→            }
   467→        }
   468→    }, true); // Use capture phase
   469→    
   470→    // Also listen for popstate
   471→    window.addEventListener('popstate', () => {
   472→        console.log('⬅️ Browser navigation detected');
   473→        runDetection();
   474→    });
   475→
   476→    // Navigation control functions
   477→    function hideCorporateNavigationItems() {
   478→        const navigationItems = document.querySelectorAll('.md-nav__link');
   479→        navigationItems.forEach(link => {
   480→            const linkText = link.textContent.trim();
   481→            // Hide items that contain corporate/BMW content indicators
   482→            if (linkText.includes('BMW Gaia LLM API') || 
   483→                linkText.includes('BMW Cloud Development Environment with Coder') ||
   484→                linkText.includes('Quick Setup') ||
   485→                linkText.includes('Testing Your Connection') ||

   493→                    console.log('Hiding corporate nav item:', linkText);

    14→This guide helps you set up LLM API access for the Agentic AI Nano-Degree course modules. Corporate users have access to pre-configured APIs, while public users can set up their own API keys.
    15→
    16→## OpenAI Setup
    17→
    18→1. Sign up at [OpenAI](https://platform.openai.com/)  
    19→2. Create an API key in your dashboard  
    20→3. Add to your `.env` file:
    21→
    22→```bash
    23→OPENAI_API_KEY=your_openai_api_key_here
    24→```
    25→
    26→## Anthropic Claude Setup
    27→
    28→1. Sign up at [Anthropic](https://console.anthropic.com/)  
    29→2. Create an API key in your console  
    30→3. Add to your `.env` file:
    31→
    32→```bash
    33→ANTHROPIC_API_KEY=your_anthropic_key_here
    34→```
    35→
    36→## Testing Your Setup

     1→# Session 10: Enterprise Integration & Production Deployment
     2→
     3→## From Innovation Labs to Production Reality: Deploying AI Agents in Corporate Infrastructure
     4→
     5→Picture this: You've built an elegant multi-agent system that can solve complex problems, coordinate workflows, and deliver intelligent insights. It works beautifully in your development environment, demos flawlessly to stakeholders, and passes every technical review. But now comes the ultimate challenge—deploying this digital intelligence into the real world of enterprise infrastructure, where security policies are non-negotiable, compliance is legally mandated, and downtime isn't just inconvenient—it's business-critical.
     6→
     7→Welcome to the world of enterprise AI deployment, where innovation meets industrial-grade infrastructure. Here, we don't just deploy agents; we integrate them into sophisticated ecosystems that must meet the rigorous standards of modern enterprise operations. Every connection is secured, every API call is monitored, every resource allocation is optimized, and every deployment must align with both technical excellence and regulatory compliance.
     8→
     9→This isn't just about Kubernetes and containers—it's about creating production-grade AI platforms that can scale from prototype to enterprise deployment while maintaining the security, reliability, and performance standards that business operations demand.
    10→
    11→*Welcome to Enterprise Integration & Production Deployment—where innovation meets industrial-grade infrastructure.*
    12→
    13→## 🎯📝⚙️ Learning Path Overview
    14→
    15→This session offers three distinct learning paths designed to match your enterprise deployment goals:
    16→
    17→=== "🎯 Observer (60-90 min)"
    18→
    19→    **Focus**: Understanding enterprise deployment architecture and cloud infrastructure
    20→    
    21→    **Activities**: Cloud platform concepts, development environment overview, security considerations
    22→    
    23→    **Ideal for**: Decision makers, architects, enterprise stakeholders
    24→
    25→=== "📝 Participant (4-6 hours)"
    26→
    27→    **Focus**: Hands-on deployment using enterprise cloud environments
    28→    
    29→    **Activities**: Workspace creation, MCP/A2A deployment, monitoring setup
    30→    
    31→    **Ideal for**: Developers, technical leads, platform engineers
    32→
    33→=== "⚙️ Implementer (12-16 hours)"
    34→
    35→    **Focus**: Complete enterprise-scale deployment with advanced configurations
    36→    
    37→    **Activities**: Custom templates, advanced security, monitoring, cost optimization
    38→    
    39→    **Ideal for**: Senior engineers, platform architects, DevOps specialists
    40→
    41→## 🎯 Observer Path: Enterprise Cloud Infrastructure Overview
    42→
    43→### The Enterprise Cloud Environment: Where Engineering Meets Innovation
    44→
    45→Modern enterprise cloud environments reflect the same precision and attention to detail that goes into any world-class operation. Just as every component in a complex system is carefully engineered, tested, and integrated into a cohesive whole, enterprise cloud infrastructure follows the same principles of excellence.
    46→
    47→### Core Infrastructure: The Foundation
    48→
    49→**Enterprise Cloud Platform**
    50→The heart of any enterprise development environment is a carefully architected cloud platform that operates within the corporate network. This isn't just a simple cloud deployment—it's a carefully designed environment that balances the flexibility developers need with the security and compliance requirements that enterprise operations demand.
    51→
    52→**Development Platform Integration**
    53→Modern development platforms serve as the developer experience layer, providing instant access to fully configured development environments. Think of it as the enterprise approach to development infrastructure—standardized, reliable, and optimized for performance.
    54→
    55→### Security Architecture: Zero-Trust by Design
    56→
    57→**Corporate Network Integration**
    58→Every connection flows through enterprise firewalls, ensuring that only authorized personnel can access development resources. Directory service integration provides seamless authentication while maintaining enterprise security standards.
    59→
    60→**VPN-Based Access**
    61→All developer access typically requires VPN connectivity, creating a secure tunnel from any location into enterprise development infrastructure. This ensures that sensitive development work remains protected regardless of where developers are working.
    62→
    63→**Compliance-First Approach**
    64→Every component is designed with regulatory compliance in mind—GDPR for data protection, industry-specific standards, and internal security policies are built into the infrastructure fabric.
    65→
    66→### The Development Platform Advantage: Excellence at Scale
    67→
    68→**Template-Driven Consistency**
    69→Standardized templates ensure that every developer starts with an identical, optimized environment. No more "it works on my machine" issues—everyone operates from the same foundation.
    70→
    71→**Resource Management**
    72→Intelligent scaling and resource allocation ensures cost optimization while providing the computational power needed for AI development. GPU resources are allocated dynamically based on workload requirements.
    73→
    74→**Tool Integration**
    75→Pre-configured access to modern development tools and AI assistants ensures that developers have cutting-edge assistance built into their workflow from day one.
    76→
    77→### Enterprise Features That Matter
    78→
    79→**Persistent Storage**
    80→Your work is never lost. Enterprise-grade storage ensures that projects, configurations, and development progress persist across sessions and scale seamlessly as projects grow.
    81→
    82→**Multi-Environment Support**
    83→From local development to production deployment, the same templates and configurations work across environments, reducing deployment complexity and risk.
    84→
    85→**Cost Transparency**
    86→Built-in cost tracking ensures that resource usage is visible and manageable, with automatic policies that prevent runaway spending while maintaining developer productivity.
    87→

   120→### Creating Your AI Agent Development Environment
   121→
   122→#### Template Selection: AI Development Environment
   123→
   124→When creating a new workspace, select the pre-configured AI development template:
   125→
   126→**Template:** Enterprise AI Development (Standard Configuration)
   127→**Configuration:**
   128→- CPU: 4 vCPUs (scalable to 16)
   129→- Memory: 16GB RAM (scalable to 64GB)
   130→- Storage: 100GB persistent storage
   131→- GPU: On-demand allocation available
   132→
   133→```yaml
   134→# workspace-config.yaml - Template configuration
   135→apiVersion: platform.enterprise.com/v1
   136→kind: Template
   137→metadata:
   138→  name: enterprise-ai-development
   139→  namespace: development
   140→spec:
   141→  displayName: "Enterprise AI Development Environment"
   142→  description: "Optimized environment for MCP/A2A development"
   143→  defaultTTL: "8h"
   144→  maxTTL: "24h"
   145→  
   146→  parameters:
   147→    - name: gpu_enabled
   148→      displayName: "Enable GPU Support"
   149→      description: "Allocate GPU resources for AI workloads"
   150→      type: bool
   151→      default: false
   152→      
   153→    - name: memory_size
   154→      displayName: "Memory Allocation"
   155→      description: "RAM allocation for the workspace"
   156→      type: string
   157→      default: "16Gi"
   158→      options:
   159→        - name: "Basic (16GB)"
   160→          value: "16Gi"
   161→        - name: "Enhanced (32GB)"
   162→          value: "32Gi"
   163→        - name: "Premium (64GB)"
   164→          value: "64Gi"
   165→```
   166→
   167→### MCP Server Deployment in Enterprise Environment
   168→
   169→#### Environment Configuration
   170→
   171→Create your MCP server configuration that integrates with enterprise infrastructure:
   172→
   173→```yaml
   174→# k8s/enterprise-mcp-deployment.yaml
   175→apiVersion: apps/v1
   176→kind: Deployment
   177→metadata:
   178→  name: enterprise-mcp-server
   179→  namespace: agentic-ai-prod
   180→  labels:
   181→    app: enterprise-mcp-server
   182→    environment: production
   183→    compliance: enterprise-standards
   184→    cost-center: ai-innovation
   185→annotations:
   186→    company.com/project: "agentic-ai-development"
   187→    company.com/owner: "ai-platform-team"
   188→spec:
   189→  replicas: 3
   190→  selector:
   191→    matchLabels:
   192→      app: enterprise-mcp-server
   193→  template:
   194→    metadata:
   195→      labels:
   196→        app: enterprise-mcp-server
   197→      annotations:
   198→        prometheus.io/scrape: "true"
   199→        prometheus.io/port: "9090"
   200→    spec:
   201→      serviceAccountName: enterprise-mcp-service-account
   202→      containers:
   203→      - name: mcp-server
   204→        image: enterprise-registry.com/mcp-server:v2.1.0
   205→        ports:
   206→        - containerPort: 8080
   207→          name: http-api
   208→        - containerPort: 9090
   209→          name: metrics
   210→        env:
   211→        # Enterprise-specific environment variables
   212→        - name: ENTERPRISE_ENVIRONMENT
   213→          value: "production"
   214→        - name: COMPLIANCE_MODE
   215→          value: "enterprise-standards"
   216→        - name: LLM_ENDPOINT
   217→          valueFrom:
   218→            configMapKeyRef:
   219→              name: enterprise-ai-config
   220→              key: llm.endpoint
   221→        - name: API_KEY
   222→          valueFrom:
   223→            secretKeyRef:
   224→              name: enterprise-ai-secrets
   225→              key: api-key
   226→        resources:
   227→          requests:
   228→            memory: "1Gi"
   229→            cpu: "500m"
   230→          limits:
   231→            memory: "4Gi"
   232→            cpu: "2000m"
   233→        # Health checks optimized for enterprise
   234→        livenessProbe:
   235→          httpGet:
   236→            path: /health/live
   237→            port: 8080
   238→          initialDelaySeconds: 120
   239→          periodSeconds: 30
   240→        readinessProbe:
   241→          httpGet:
   242→            path: /health/ready
   243→            port: 8080
   244→          initialDelaySeconds: 60
   245→          periodSeconds: 15
   246→        # Security context
   247→        securityContext:
   248→          runAsNonRoot: true
   249→          runAsUser: 1001
   250→          allowPrivilegeEscalation: false
   251→          readOnlyRootFilesystem: true
   252→```

   259→# k8s/enterprise-a2a-orchestrator.yaml

   286→          value: "enterprise"

   288→          value: "high"

   441→    let lastUrl = location.href;

   443→        const url = location.href;

   453→    });

### Assistant

You're absolutely correct on all points:

1. **Architecture Understanding**: There are indeed two ways to access corporate content:
   - **Development**: Git submodule brings unencrypted files to authorized users' local machines
   - **Published Site**: Dynamic CN detection decrypts encrypted content for corporate network users

2. **Hostname Restrictions Were Wrong**: The logic should ALWAYS attempt CN detection regardless of hostname. If someone is on the corporate network, they should get corporate content whether they're on:
   - `github.io` (published site)
   - `localhost` (local development)
   - `fwornle.github.io` (your personal domain)

3. **Encrypted File Location**: You're right to question this. The encrypted corporate content should be in the public repo so it gets built into the published GitHub Pages site, where the JavaScript can decrypt it for corporate network users.

4. **Test Mode Was Wrong**: The temporary test parameter I added was indeed wrong - it would allow anyone to bypass security by adding a URL parameter.

Now the system works correctly:
- **Always runs CN detection** via IP check and internal service check
- **No hostname-based restrictions** - corporate users get corporate content everywhere
- **Security through CN detection only** - if you can't reach BMW internal services, you get public content

The current behavior you're seeing (public content on localhost) is actually correct - since you're testing locally without VPN access to BMW internal services, the CN detection fails and shows public content as intended.

    20→         * Derives the same key used for encryption

    22→        async deriveKey(passphrase) {
    23→            const encoder = new TextEncoder();
    24→            const data = encoder.encode(passphrase);
    25→            const hashBuffer = await crypto.subtle.digest('SHA-256', data);
    26→            return await crypto.subtle.importKey(
    27→                'raw',
    28→                hashBuffer,
    29→                { name: 'AES-GCM' },
    30→                false,
    31→                ['decrypt']
    32→            );
    33→        }

    43→                
    44→                // Combine encrypted data with auth tag for AES-GCM
    45→                const ciphertext = new Uint8Array(encrypted.byteLength + authTag.byteLength);
    46→                ciphertext.set(new Uint8Array(encrypted), 0);
    47→                ciphertext.set(new Uint8Array(authTag), encrypted.byteLength);
    48→
    49→                const decrypted = await crypto.subtle.decrypt(
    50→                    {

    69→        base64ToArrayBuffer(base64) {

    73→                bytes[i] = binaryString.charCodeAt(i);

   140→        /**
   141→         * Injects decrypted markdown content
   142→         */
   143→        async injectMarkdownContent(filePath, content) {
   144→            // Look for elements that reference this file path
   145→            const selector = `[href*="${filePath}"], [src*="${filePath}"]`;
   146→            const elements = document.querySelectorAll(selector);
   147→            
   148→            if (elements.length > 0) {
   149→                console.log(`💉 Injecting markdown content for ${filePath}`);
   150→                // Convert markdown to HTML and inject
   151→                // This would require a markdown parser or server-side rendering
   152→                // For now, just log that content is available
   153→                console.log(`📄 Content available for ${filePath} (${content.length} chars)`);
   154→            }
   155→        }
   156→
   157→        /**
   158→         * Injects decrypted image content
   159→         */
   160→        async injectImageContent(filePath, base64Content) {
   161→            // Find img elements with src pointing to this file
   162→            const images = document.querySelectorAll(`img[src*="${filePath}"]`);
   163→            
   164→            images.forEach(img => {
   165→                try {
   166→                    // Determine image type from file extension
   167→                    const extension = filePath.split('.').pop().toLowerCase();
   168→                    const mimeType = this.getMimeType(extension);
   169→                    
   170→                    // Create data URL from base64 content
   171→                    const dataUrl = `data:${mimeType};base64,${base64Content}`;
   172→                    
   173→                    console.log(`🖼️ Injecting image: ${filePath}`);
   174→                    img.src = dataUrl;
   175→                } catch (error) {
   176→                    console.error(`Failed to inject image ${filePath}:`, error);
   177→                }
   178→            });
   179→        }
   180→
   181→        /**
   182→         * Gets MIME type for image extensions
   183→         */
   184→        getMimeType(extension) {
   185→            const mimeTypes = {
   186→                'png': 'image/png',
   187→                'jpg': 'image/jpeg',
   188→                'jpeg': 'image/jpeg',
   189→                'gif': 'image/gif',
   190→                'svg': 'image/svg+xml'
   191→            };
   192→            return mimeTypes[extension] || 'image/png';
   193→        }
   194→
   195→        /**
   196→         * Test decryption with the test file

### Assistant

I can see the issue now. The corporate content loader is designed to inject content but the current approach is incomplete. The system needs to:

1. **Replace the entire page content** with the decrypted corporate version
2. **Not just inject images** but replace the whole markdown content

For the coder page specifically, when corporate network is detected, it should replace the entire page content with the decrypted `00_intro/coder-detailed.md` content.

### Assistant

**Tool:** Edit
**Input:** ```json
{
  "file_path": "/Users/q284340/Agentic/nano-degree/docs-content/javascripts/corporate-content-loader.js",
  "old_string": "        /**\n         * Injects decrypted markdown content\n         */\n        async injectMarkdownContent(filePath, content) {\n            // Look for elements that reference this file path\n            const selector = `[href*=\"${filePath}\"], [src*=\"${filePath}\"]`;\n            const elements = document.querySelectorAll(selector);\n            \n            if (elements.length > 0) {\n                console.log(`💉 Injecting markdown content for ${filePath}`);\n                // Convert markdown to HTML and inject\n                // This would require a markdown parser or server-side rendering\n                // For now, just log that content is available\n                console.log(`📄 Content available for ${filePath} (${content.length} chars)`);\n            }\n        }",
  "new_string": "        /**\n         * Replaces the main page content with corporate markdown content\n         */\n        async replacePageContent(markdownContent) {\n            try {\n                // Find the main content area - MkDocs uses .md-content__inner\n                const contentArea = document.querySelector('.md-content__inner') || \n                                   document.querySelector('main') || \n                                   document.querySelector('article');\n                \n                if (!contentArea) {\n                    console.error('Could not find main content area to replace');\n                    return;\n                }\n                \n                console.log('🔄 Replacing main content area with corporate content');\n                \n                // Simple markdown to HTML conversion for key elements\n                let htmlContent = markdownContent\n                    .replace(/^# (.+)$/gm, '<h1>$1</h1>')\n                    .replace(/^## (.+)$/gm, '<h2>$1</h2>')\n                    .replace(/^### (.+)$/gm, '<h3>$1</h3>')\n                    .replace(/^#### (.+)$/gm, '<h4>$1</h4>')\n                    .replace(/\\*\\*(.+?)\\*\\*/g, '<strong>$1</strong>')\n                    .replace(/\\*(.+?)\\*/g, '<em>$1</em>')\n                    .replace(/`(.+?)`/g, '<code>$1</code>')\n                    .replace(/\\[(.+?)\\]\\((.+?)\\)/g, '<a href=\"$2\">$1</a>')\n                    .replace(/!\\[(.+?)\\]\\((.+?)\\)/g, '<img src=\"$2\" alt=\"$1\">')\n                    .replace(/^- (.+)$/gm, '<li>$1</li>')\n                    .replace(/(<li>.*<\\/li>)/s, '<ul>$1</ul>')\n                    .replace(/^(\\d+)\\. (.+)$/gm, '<li>$2</li>')\n                    .replace(/```(\\w+)?\\n([\\s\\S]*?)```/g, '<pre><code class=\"language-$1\">$2</code></pre>')\n                    .replace(/\\n\\n/g, '</p><p>')\n                    .replace(/^(?!<[h1-6]|<ul|<ol|<pre|<script)(.+)$/gm, '<p>$1</p>')\n                    .replace(/<p><\\/p>/g, '');\n                \n                // Replace the content\n                contentArea.innerHTML = htmlContent;\n                \n                console.log('✅ Corporate content successfully injected into page');\n                \n            } catch (error) {\n                console.error('❌ Failed to replace page content:', error);\n            }\n        }\n\n        /**\n         * Injects decrypted markdown content (legacy method, kept for compatibility)\n         */\n        async injectMarkdownContent(filePath, content) {\n            // Look for elements that reference this file path\n            const selector = `[href*=\"${filePath}\"], [src*=\"${filePath}\"]`;\n            const elements = document.querySelectorAll(selector);\n            \n            if (elements.length > 0) {\n                console.log(`💉 Injecting markdown content for ${filePath}`);\n                // Convert markdown to HTML and inject\n                // This would require a markdown parser or server-side rendering\n                // For now, just log that content is available\n                console.log(`📄 Content available for ${filePath} (${content.length} chars)`);\n            }\n        }"

   160→            try {
   161→                // Find the main content area - MkDocs uses .md-content__inner
   162→                const contentArea = document.querySelector('.md-content__inner') || 
   163→                                   document.querySelector('main') || 
   164→                                   document.querySelector('article');
   165→

   175→                    .replace(/^# (.+)$/gm, '<h1>$1</h1>')
   176→                    .replace(/^## (.+)$/gm, '<h2>$1</h2>')
   177→                    .replace(/^### (.+)$/gm, '<h3>$1</h3>')
   178→                    .replace(/^#### (.+)$/gm, '<h4>$1</h4>')
   179→                    .replace(/\*\*(.+?)\*\*/g, '<strong>$1</strong>')
   180→                    .replace(/\*(.+?)\*/g, '<em>$1</em>')
   181→                    .replace(/`(.+?)`/g, '<code>$1</code>')
   182→                    .replace(/\[(.+?)\]\((.+?)\)/g, '<a href="$2">$1</a>')

   184→                    .replace(/^- (.+)$/gm, '<li>$1</li>')

   186→                    .replace(/^(\d+)\. (.+)$/gm, '<li>$2</li>')

   193→                contentArea.innerHTML = htmlContent;
